<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4a420d8e-663f-41a2-accd-c8a39a3da3b5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6454009387387057258">Dying sucks<br/>...and high school senior Ember McWilliams knows firsthand. <br/><br/>After a fatal car accident, her gifted little sister brought her back.   <span id="freeText6454009387387057258" style="display:none">Dying sucks<br />...and high school senior Ember McWilliams knows firsthand. <br /><br />After a fatal car accident, her gifted little sister brought her back. Now anything Ember touches dies. And that, well, really blows.<br /><br />Ember operates on a no-touch policy with all living things--including boys. When Hayden Cromwell shows up, quoting Oscar Wilde and claiming her curse is a gift, she thinks he's a crazed cutie. But when he tells her he can help control it, she's more than interested. There's just one catch: Ember has to trust Hayden's adopted father, a man she's sure has sinister reasons for collecting children whose abilities even weird her out. However, she's willing to do anything to hold her sister's hand again. And hell, she'd also like to be able to kiss Hayden. Who wouldn't?<br /><br />But when Ember learns the accident that turned her into a freak may not've been an accident at all, she's not sure who to trust. Someone wanted her dead, and the closer she gets to the truth, the closer she is to losing not only her heart, but her life.<br /><br /> For real this time.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206076994" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1206076994?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781937053123" href="/book/show/17179853-cursed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206076994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10182252065918533759"><b> 4 Cursed stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> "You have a soul. You aren’t evil. There’s nothing you can say that will make me think that." </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/cursed.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424591896i/13781049.png' alt=' photo cursed.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Jennifer Armentrout is one of my all time favorite authors. JLA doesn't write within the typical book formula and marches to the beat of her own drummer, which is refreshing in this day and age of publishing. Whether she is writing young adult, new adult, or thrillers, I have liked or loved everything she's ever written. <b> Cursed </b> is not exception, coming in at one of her most und</span>
  <span id="freeText10182252065918533759" style="display:none"><b> 4 Cursed stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> "You have a soul. You aren’t evil. There’s nothing you can say that will make me think that." </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/cursed.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424591896i/13781049.png" alt=" photo cursed.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Jennifer Armentrout is one of my all time favorite authors. JLA doesn't write within the typical book formula and marches to the beat of her own drummer, which is refreshing in this day and age of publishing. Whether she is writing young adult, new adult, or thrillers, I have liked or loved everything she's ever written. <b> Cursed </b> is not exception, coming in at one of her most underrated books, and one I thoroughly enjoyed.<br><br><b> Cursed </b> is the story of teenager Ember. Ember died two years before in a car accident with her dad when her then three year old sister Olivia brought her back from the dead. Olivia wasn't able to save their father, and their mother seems to have gone into a catatonic shock since then and doesn't talk to anyone. And the weirdest thing about being brought back from the dead? Any living thing that touches Ember's skin dies. Plants, animals, and humans. So for two years Ember has lived as the town freak with scars covering her body and doing her best to avoid human interaction. <br><br>Suddenly, Ember and her family are abducted by Jonathon Cromwell, a man who claims to have their best interests at heart, and he brings them to a home full of kids with special abilities. It is made clear that Olivia is in fact the only member of the family he wants, and Ember and her mother are expendable. At this house, Ember's only friend is Hayden, Jonathan's adopted son. Hayden seems to be the only one on Ember's team, and she deals daily with the fact that she is in a home where she isn't wanted.<br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/pagebreak.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421135336i/13327545.png" alt=" photo pagebreak.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Reading a JLA book is a comfort thing for me and even though she's written a shit ton of books, I'm down to like 2 books I haven't read by her yet. I'd been putting this book off for a while but decided it was time to give it a shot. I went into this book with fairly low expectations since not many people seem to have read it, and the average Goodreads rating is below a 4.0. <br><br>While the character of Ember could be a bit whiny and impulsive sometimes, her struggle was very relatable to readers of this book. I think I can speak for everyone and say we've all felt like an outcast at some point in our lives, or even like we didn't belong somewhere, and this was an issue Ember dealt with every day of her life, and everywhere she went. Constantly second guessing herself, wondering if she even had a soul once she was brought back, not able to have the smallest amount of human contact without fear of hurting someone; I got to say, I'm kind of amazed she didn't have a breakdown holding herself and her feelings together. To me, this made her strong.<br><br>Hayden was such a great book boyfriend. He also proves that JLA has been writing great heroes since the beginning of her published writing career. His faith in Ember was amazing and I kind of wish guys like him existed in my real life world.<br><br><b> <i> “My brain must have felt sorry for me, so it’d created the only type of guy I could touch—a fantasy one.” </i> </b><br><br>There were a few inconsistencies which is why I can't rate this book a 5. For example, Ember's change in eye color was never fully explained, and I really would have liked an epilogue to see if certain aspects of Ember's power worked out or not. Plus, the entire book The Facility was a huge motif and we never even saw it as a reader. But these things did not take away from my enjoyment of the book.<br><br>So if you are looking for a fun yet deep young adult paranormal book, this one is for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10182252065918533759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3081394051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3081394051" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3081394051?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3081394051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2642410712023981399"><b>“My brain must have felt sorry for me, so it’d created the only type of guy I could touch—a fantasy one.”</b> <br/><br/><i>#RELATABLE</i><br/><br/>This <i>would've been</i> a <b>five-star review</b>, but there were just so many...<i>unresolved issues</i>? Was this meant to be the beginning of a new series or...? I mean, yes, for the most part, the main story arc of the book is <b>wrapped up</b>, but there were still so many unanswered questions. It's honestly a shame because I would've <i>LOVED</i> to have had a series revolved around these characters.<br/><br/>For all </span>
  <span id="freeText2642410712023981399" style="display:none"><b>“My brain must have felt sorry for me, so it’d created the only type of guy I could touch—a fantasy one.”</b> <br /><br /><i>#RELATABLE</i><br /><br />This <i>would've been</i> a <b>five-star review</b>, but there were just so many...<i>unresolved issues</i>? Was this meant to be the beginning of a new series or...? I mean, yes, for the most part, the main story arc of the book is <b>wrapped up</b>, but there were still so many unanswered questions. It's honestly a shame because I would've <i>LOVED</i> to have had a series revolved around these characters.<br /><br />For all the reviews that called this an <b>X-Men/Shatter Me</b> concoction, they weren't wrong. Some people have been endowed with a "<b>gift</b>" in this world. After a fatal car accident, <b>Ember</b>'s little sister, <b>Olivia</b>, brought her <i>back from the dead</i>. But she didn't just come back to life...she also came back with the ability to <i>kill whatever she touches</i>. Fast forward a few years, and in swoops <b>Jonathan Cromwell</b>, who whisks them away to their home, a safe haven for other "gifted" people, including his adopted son, <b>Hayden</b>. <br /><br />Like Juliette from <i>Shatter Me</i>, I really empathised with Ember because she was so <b>traumatised</b> and <b>emotionally shut down</b> from the aftermath of the accident, and was practically raising her little sister, since her dad died in the accident and her mum was basically a vegetable, who didn't even acknowledge her existence. <br /><br />Hayden was such a change from JLA's usual dark and broody alpha male types (Lux, anyone?). He was just so <b>sweet and genuine</b>, and his background was as equally heartbreaking as Ember's. They truly <i>healed each other</i>, and their relationship was so pure. <b>I love them so much. &lt;3</b><br /><br />I really enjoyed this, but I wish that it had either been <i>longer</i>, so that everything was completely wrapped up, or that it had been <i>continued as a series</i>. I also wish that the antagonist had been a tad <i>less predictable</i>. But regardless, <b>I loved this book</b> and completed it in one sitting. It's definitely one of JLA's <i>under-appreciated books</i>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18197908329064529810">Ok. Not a bad book, but it feels like Armentrout planned on making this into a series, and then...<i><b>didn't</b>?</i><br/>So, yeah. While the ending <i>ends</i>, it still feels like there are too many loose threads dangling for the book to be <i>over-over</i>. But...I mean, whatever. <br/>That's fine, right?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461073342ra/18819616.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Heh. <br/>Anyway, the basic gist of the story is that Ember has this Poison Touch power. If someone even brushes up against her bare skin, they're screwed.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461075566ra/18820299.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So how did this happen?<br/>Well, her entire family was in a car accident, in whi</span>
  <span id="freeText18197908329064529810" style="display:none">Ok. Not a bad book, but it feels like Armentrout planned on making this into a series, and then...<i><b>didn't</b>?</i><br>So, yeah. While the ending <i>ends</i>, it still feels like there are too many loose threads dangling for the book to be <i>over-over</i>. But...I mean, whatever. <br>That's fine, right?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461073342ra/18819616.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Heh. <br>Anyway, the basic gist of the story is that Ember has this Poison Touch power. If someone even brushes up against her bare skin, they're screwed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461075566ra/18820299.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So how did this happen?<br>Well, her entire family was in a car accident, in which Ember and her father were both killed. Now, her little sister has the power to bring people back from the dead, so <b>Ta-da!</b>, Ember is still among the living.<br>Unfortunately, their dad was super-duper dead, so there was no bringing him back...I guess.<br>Alrighty, a few days after the accident, Ember starts to realize that everything she touches (pets, plants, etc.) die within seconds of coming into contact with her skin.<br><i>Lucky for the paramedics, doctors, and nurses who treated her, the spooky Death Fingers thing didn't kick in immediately after being resuscitated.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461075566ra/18820300.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Ok, so flash forward a bit, and Ember is trying to raise her little sister (because mom has gone crazy), she's being bullied in high school, and they are quickly running out of money.<br>Long story short, her life suuuuuuuucks.<br><b>Enter Shady Professor Xavier &amp; his team of mutant superheros!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461077016ra/18820658.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately, even among the weirdos, she's is an outcast. Except for that One Special Boy who loves her juuuuuuuust as she is...<br>So will <s>Rogue</s> Ember learn to control her gift &amp; find twue wuv?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461077016ra/18820659.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, that's not <i>exactly</i> the entire plot, because there's questions surrounding the accident that gave her powers, a whole lotta questions quasi-evil place called the Facility, and serious questions about the leader of this group of super-kids.<br><b>But.</b><br>None of that stuff ever gets real answers. <div id="review_984106865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984106865" />
    <a title="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10376232-saania-zee-jamal"><img alt="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495529362p2/10376232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" href="/user/show/10376232-saania-zee-jamal">Saania Zee Jamal ϟ</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=can-you-feel-the-chemistry">can-you-feel-the-chemistry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=give-it-a-break-woman">give-it-a-break-woman</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984106865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5633816864881409936">That horribly corny ending did it in for me- there's just no way I can give this book more than two stars.<br/><br/>Jennifer gave me the feeling that she simply couldn't bother cooking up a more satisfying finish (because merlin knows she's definitely capable of it with all her wonders) and tying up loose ends, and that disappointed me so much to the extent that Hayden and Ember's once thrilling romance build-up now just pissed me off with their immensely cheestastic I Love You's. <s>Seriously, I'm drowning </s></span>
  <span id="freeText5633816864881409936" style="display:none">That horribly corny ending did it in for me- there's just no way I can give this book more than two stars.<br /><br />Jennifer gave me the feeling that she simply couldn't bother cooking up a more satisfying finish (because merlin knows she's definitely capable of it with all her wonders) and tying up loose ends, and that disappointed me so much to the extent that Hayden and Ember's once thrilling romance build-up now just pissed me off with their immensely cheestastic I Love You's. <s>Seriously, I'm drowning in all the cheddar here!</s><br /><br />It would have been much appreciated if we'd gotten an insight into all the other things at hand: how things would progress from here, if Ember could grasp more control over her 'gift', character development for every single other bloody person who wasn't <i>Hayden</i> (hell, maybe even him)<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and WHO IN FACT HAD WIPED HER MOTHER'S MEMORY AWAY?????? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Honestly, I'm not even asking for a sequel here (not in a gazillion years), just an epilogue of sorts would have left me quite satisfied. But alas, it's the <i>breathtaking</i>, <i>the intense</i>, the <i>majestic</i>, the <b>
  <i>LURRRVE</i>
</b> between the two protagonists that must always prevail!<br /><br />*exaggerated eye rolling*</span>
  <a data-text-id="5633816864881409936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421420352" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421420352" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/344616-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421420352?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/344616-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/344616-rachel?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/344616-rachel?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer421420352&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421420352" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13490788274449560716">So many issues, so, so many issues I hardly know where to start. First off, I guess I should preface my review by saying I like Obsidian and Onyx, and Jennifer Armentrout's Lux series. They are what drew me to Cursed in the first place. I think they're fun, have great characters, and a good plot. I also think Armentrout is a good storyteller. Her books draw you in and make you want to keep reading, so I will absolutely keep reading other books by her. <br/><br/>But.<br/><br/>Yes, there is a but. <br/><br/>This book drove me </span>
  <span id="freeText13490788274449560716" style="display:none">So many issues, so, so many issues I hardly know where to start. First off, I guess I should preface my review by saying I like Obsidian and Onyx, and Jennifer Armentrout's Lux series. They are what drew me to Cursed in the first place. I think they're fun, have great characters, and a good plot. I also think Armentrout is a good storyteller. Her books draw you in and make you want to keep reading, so I will absolutely keep reading other books by her. <br /><br />But.<br /><br />Yes, there is a but. <br /><br />This book drove me absolutely crazy. You can ask my family, it honestly put me in a bad mood. And this book is supposed to be a stand alone. If it was a series, I would probably like it better, but the ending was horrible---Be warned, from here on out, I'm giving away basically the whole plot, so there are tons and tons of spoilers. If you don't want to know, don't keep reading, but I can't review this without giving some major stuff away---I'm sorry, but so you killed the crazy guy trying to kill you? That's nice, but you're still living with a family of creepers who kidnapped you and mind-wiped your best friend. How is that possibly okay?<br /><br />Okay, I'll back up. First off Ember gets kidnapped along with her little sister. Then Cromwell and his "family" tell her, if you can't accept living her with us, not giving away our secrets, and not trying to run away, we will keep your sister and send you to "The Facility," basically a place where the government locks up and trains (read: tortures) kids with gifts. Then when she tells her best friend she is staying with family (because she isn't stupid enough to tell him she was kidnapped by a crazy family of paranormals) and he comes to visit her because he is worried (I mean, she left suddenly, aka was kidnapped), they wipe his mind of all his memories of her. Then they get mad at her for not telling them that she told her friend where she was staying, claiming the mind-wipe thing it is all her fault. <br /><br />And in the end, these people are supposed to be the good guys? I'm sorry, but in what universe could they ever be construed as decent human beings? Oh, wait, I guess they don't even think of themselves as human. In fact, they don't eat lunch with humans, or really associate with them at all because they're "gifted." If they were good, why didn't they talk to Ember straight up instead of kidnapping her in the beginning? She was desperate, and the home they took her to could have been a refuge, but I guess where's the drama in that?<br /><br />Then there's Ember's love interest, Hayden. Yes, he is sweet to her and gorgeous and tries to help her control her curse/gift, but he also believes that the mind-wipe thing was justified, blaming Ember for not telling him, and he stalked her for two years. I get that he is a broken boy and is drawn to Ember because of everything she suffers, but how could Ember ever really fall in love with him when he supports the his adopted father and helps kidnap Ember? Can you say Stockholm syndrome? <br /><br />Plus, he still sympathizes with his empathic "sister," Phoebe, who put dead bunnies, nooses, and models of the car-crash that killed Ember and her father in Ember's locker because she doesn't like her. You would think since Phoebe can literally feel how miserable Ember is, she might try and help a little, but no. Let's just scare the girl into running away or being taken by the Facility. Yeah, lovely family of creepers we have here.<br /><br />Now to the ending. Okay, so throughout the book someone has been trying to kill Ember. Finally she gets kidnapped, big stuff is revealed, mysteries solved, etc. But not really. Yes, Ember kills the bad guy before he kills her, and everyone discovers she has partial control of her gift. But she also finds out that Cromwell tried to train someone else with her exact gift years before and failed. He "tried" so hard to help and did horrible things that caused the girl to commit suicide. Then, when the Facility tries to take Ember away, he doesn't let them, stating,"She's mine now. And she's very important." Does it get any creepier than that. I mean, the girl who can kill with a touch is his and very important?<br /><br />But in the end this is supposed to be okay? Cromwell tells her he would have never sent her to the Facility, though he threatened her with it earlier in the book. So am I supposed to believe that Ember's life is going to be great now. Yes, she can kiss her beautiful boyfriend for almost a minute now (which is how the book ends), but she is still basically being held captive by a creeper family. The absolute only difference in her situation now is that she is in love with one of them, and she has partial control of her ability. Oh, and they didn't kill her father. That's it. The mind-wipe thing is never addressed again, and suddenly they look so much better because someone worse kidnapped her from her kidnappers? Yes, let's introduce another villain so we can pretend the love interest and his family aren't a bunch of crazy psychopaths.<br /><br />The worst part about this book is that there isn't a sequel. If there were, I would think that all these issues would be taken care of or at least addressed. I would be okay with the ending, probably even her being with Hayden, because obviously the author would, after a lot of struggles, pull out some kind of escape or punishment or mind-wipe and leave us with a slightly less creepy ending. As it is, why is Ember happy? Because she is in love, and therefore all is forgiven? I don't get it.<br /><br />As far as writing goes, this book is probably 3 stars for me. Obviously Jennifer Armentrout drew me into the story and made me feel things (mostly frustration and irritation, but at lest she made me feel things and care about the Ember). As far as how much I liked the book though . . . 1 star. I'm sorry, but I just couldn't get over the aforementioned issues. I know most people like this book, and that's fine. I really wanted to as well, but I couldn't. <br /><br />First reviewed on my blog: <a href="http://rachels-reads.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel's Reads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13490788274449560716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_224110456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224110456" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224110456?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224110456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17734114769588359970">3.5 Stars<br/><br/>Ember McWilliams feels cursed. I think I would feel the same way if I had her ability. Two years ago she was in a car accident in which she died and was brought back to life by her little sister, Olivia. Ever since then her touch kills any living thing. She goes around with gloves to prevent any accidents but also to cover scars all over her arms left by the accident. As if that wasn’t enough, her normally brown eyes were turned sky blue after the accident. Ember once was a popular outg</span>
  <span id="freeText17734114769588359970" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br /><br />Ember McWilliams feels cursed. I think I would feel the same way if I had her ability. Two years ago she was in a car accident in which she died and was brought back to life by her little sister, Olivia. Ever since then her touch kills any living thing. She goes around with gloves to prevent any accidents but also to cover scars all over her arms left by the accident. As if that wasn’t enough, her normally brown eyes were turned sky blue after the accident. Ember once was a popular outgoing normal girl in school and now because of the changes, is ridiculed and treated like a freak at school. School isn’t the only challenge in Ember’s life though. Her father was killed in the accident and her mother is basically catatonic, leaving Ember to care for Olivia, who is now five years old. Talk about being dealt some bad cards! Ember starts seeing a mysterious boy, Hayden, show up all over the place, seeming to know way more about her than she does of him. Okay, he’s sort of gorgeous, but that doesn’t make it any less creepy! <br /><br />For two years Ember has managed to keep things together but after an ex-boyfriend, and now bully, backs Ember into a corner and pretty much assaults her, he dies from her touch. Hayden and an unknown group steps in to cover the accident, and takes her whole family in. Well, maybe not takes in as much as kidnaps. Ember does not go willingly, and they don’t care. Turns out there are others with special abilities that all live together as a family with Hayden’s father, Jonathan Cromwell as the leader. Olivia couldn’t be happier and bonds with this “family” immediately. Ember is a different story though, because of her ability, none of the others besides Hayden want her there. Ember is drawn to Hayden, understandably so because he is basically her only friend and advocate. Sparks fly between these two, but she wonders if she can trust him with his obvious devotion to his father. Ember is completely suspicious of Mr. Cromwell’s intentions, and he’s not so friendly to her either. Then, Ember discovers there may be more to her “accident” two years ago and no longer knows who to trust. <br /><br />I really felt bad for Ember. She really had her life go down the toilet, and then had to shoulder such great responsibility on top of coping with her power. The members of the Cromwell house, with the exception of Hayden, Parker and Ms. Liz, are downright rude to her. Phoebe, the twin sister to Parker, really got under my skin. I thought she was a hateful, jealous, witch! I can’t imagine living a life where you couldn’t touch another living being. How horrible would that be?! Hayden has a power that helps with that issue, but I don’t want to say anymore and give anything away. I really liked Hayden in this story! The fact that he made it his goal to make Ember feel welcome and normal again totally won me over. Well that and of course some swoon-worthy scenes! Here’s one that got my blood pumping in anticipation:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Hayden opened his eyes. “Em….?” His stare held so much intensity that I found it difficult to breath. A look of yearning, of desperation, and he was studying me. Studying my face, the way my top had slipped down. And is stare was spreading a hot flush over my body. Slowly, he dipped down, placing his weight on one arm. He brought his hand to the side of my face, his fingers hovering over my cheek. My own fingers curled into the sweater. God, I wanted him to touch me so badly. The need consumed me—burned like fire. </i>
</b><br /><br />I’ll leave you to wonder whether he touches her or not! <br /><br />While I enjoyed Cursed and had a lot of fun reading it, it’s not my favorite of Jennifer L. Armentrout’s. With that said, I still think any JLA fan will still enjoy this story, as I did. If the first half was as engrossing as the second, I would’ve rated this higher; it just dragged <i>a little</i> in the beginning. Also, while the mystery does wrap up in this book I felt like we could have more to this story. I was a little surprised that this is a stand-alone. Unless someone knows something I don’t. But don’t worry; it doesn’t leave off on a bad note or anything. <br /><br />I just want to shout out a thank you to my wonderful blogger friend, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1894085-alexa" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexa</a><br />over at <a href="http://collections-books.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Collections</a> for lending me her copy! She’s a book lover’s dream-friend! <br /> <br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2012/08/review-cursed-by-jennifer-l-armentrout.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17734114769588359970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3002600786" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93273793-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566527951p2/93273793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3002600786?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/93273793-grace">Grace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3002600786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4421358406464878676">This was a tough read.<br/>The main character, Ember was absolutely helpless, vulnerable and picked on throughout this book. <br/>The painful scenes were never ending. She didn’t feel like she belonged in school, she was bullied, she didn’t have answers to the mystery that surrounds the accident that claimed her father’s life, she blamed herself for everything, she has a death touch, and on top of that, someone wants her dead and have attempted to do so more than once. <br/>It was hard to read because she coul</span>
  <span id="freeText4421358406464878676" style="display:none">This was a tough read.<br />The main character, Ember was absolutely helpless, vulnerable and picked on throughout this book. <br />The painful scenes were never ending. She didn’t feel like she belonged in school, she was bullied, she didn’t have answers to the mystery that surrounds the accident that claimed her father’s life, she blamed herself for everything, she has a death touch, and on top of that, someone wants her dead and have attempted to do so more than once. <br />It was hard to read because she couldn’t fight back, she was completely helpless through the series of painful experiences.<br />The moral of the story is, we can sometimes confuse our gifts for curses, and that almost always makes us a prey for bullies. We need to embrace who we are, let people in, then we will see what gifts 🎁 we are to the world 🌎.</span>

<div id="review_1258988063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1258988063" />
    <a title="Sinead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13986510-sinead"><img alt="Sinead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602449961p2/13986510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1258988063?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sinead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sinead" href="/user/show/13986510-sinead">Sinead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=heartbreakingly-romantic">heartbreakingly-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=sad">sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13986510-sinead?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1258988063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9172240805478388539">It’s my unofficial booknerd mission to read every single one of Jen’s books. I’m up to date on all her latest releases, so let’s step back five years: to 2012, which was when this book was released. I was a little worried, as Jen has improved loads as a writer and I thought the writing wouldn’t be as good, but I was wrong! This was, just like the rest of Jen’s books, really enjoyable. <br/><br/>It tells the story of Ember. At first, you think she’s just an ordinary high school student, but then you discov</span>
  <span id="freeText9172240805478388539" style="display:none">It’s my unofficial booknerd mission to read every single one of Jen’s books. I’m up to date on all her latest releases, so let’s step back five years: to 2012, which was when this book was released. I was a little worried, as Jen has improved loads as a writer and I thought the writing wouldn’t be as good, but I was wrong! This was, just like the rest of Jen’s books, really enjoyable. <br /><br />It tells the story of Ember. At first, you think she’s just an ordinary high school student, but then you discover that she’s had a unique experience: she’s died, and was brought back to life. This was due to her five year old sister’s unusual ability to bring back the dead. When Ember was in a car crash with her family two years ago, Ember’s survival seemed miraculous, especially since her father died. But his death knocked Ember’s mother to the core, and now she can’t get out of bed to take care of her children.<br /><br />So it’s been Ember’s responsibility to be both a parent and a sister to Olivia, and it’s taking its toll on her. Especially since when Ember was brought back, she was got this mysterious ability that means she will kill anything she touches. Pets, plants, even people. Ember’s life is incredibly tough as she alienates herself from her classmates and struggles to accept the hand she’s been dealt, when suddenly, her life changes drastically again! A man called Jonathan Cromwell takes in Ember, Olivia and her mother, stating that his home full of people with different gifts, like Ember and Olivia, so that they will be safe and taken care of. This house also includes Hayden, who really impacts Ember’s life, and he says he knows her, understands her and just wants to help her. <br /><br />But after two years of hating her “gift” and avoiding people at all costs, why should Ember trust any of them? She’s not gifted, she’s cursed. And why does she suddenly get the feeling that these people also have something to do with the infamous car accident?<br /><br />This book constantly had me wondering who could be trusted, or couldn’t, just for something to happen for everything to change again. Ember went through so much, and I don’t blame her for not believing she could control her gift after constantly being told what a freak she was. She and Hayden were really cute as well.<br /><br />The only thing I didn’t like was the fact that Hayden was a little bit obsessed with her and the only reason he has for why was because she felt bad for her. <br /><br />Other than that, I would recommend this book if you’re a fan of Jennifer L Armentrout like I am.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9172240805478388539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_238226109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238226109" />
    <a title="Julianna Helms" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5835325-julianna-helms"><img alt="Julianna Helms" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372835701p2/5835325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238226109?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna Helms" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna Helms" href="/user/show/5835325-julianna-helms">Julianna Helms</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=arc-tours">arc-tours</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=skimmed-like-milk-jk">skimmed-like-milk-jk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=rockin-the-minority-yo">rockin-the-minority-yo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=way-too-cliche">way-too-cliche</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238226109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5986091380670976825"><s><b>Quick Reaction:</b> I feel kind of bad about the two-stars thing. But the truth is, <i>Cursed</i> was at best just a mere <i>okay</i> for me...</s><br/><br/><b>**Actual, full review**</b> Original is <a href='http://thereviewsnews.blogspot.com/2012/08/cursed-and-why-sometimes-disappointment.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here on my blog</a>. (Note: due to copy-and-paste, most formatting and links have been lost.)<br/><br/>If you are a frequent reader of book blogs, you're probably more-than-familiar with Jennifer L. Armentrout. She wrote the Covenant and Obsidian series, both of which are quite the hit, especially among bloggers. So I would like to preface this review</span>
  <span id="freeText5986091380670976825" style="display:none"><s><b>Quick Reaction:</b> I feel kind of bad about the two-stars thing. But the truth is, <i>Cursed</i> was at best just a mere <i>okay</i> for me...</s><br /><br /><b>**Actual, full review**</b> Original is <a href="http://thereviewsnews.blogspot.com/2012/08/cursed-and-why-sometimes-disappointment.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here on my blog</a>. (Note: due to copy-and-paste, most formatting and links have been lost.)<br /><br />If you are a frequent reader of book blogs, you're probably more-than-familiar with Jennifer L. Armentrout. She wrote the Covenant and Obsidian series, both of which are quite the hit, especially among bloggers. So I would like to preface this review with a giant sign:<br /><br /><b>THIS IS NOT A POSITIVE REVIEW. IT'S ALSO SEMI-LONG. READ ON AT YOUR OWN RISK.</b><br /><br />Awesome. Now that we've got that out of the way, let's continue, shall we?<br /><br />Here's the thing: I love me some Jen Armentrout. She's really nice and awesome and <a href="http://thereviewsnews.blogspot.com/2011/11/you-wanna-know-whats-up-with-aliens.html" rel="nofollow noopener">I thoroughly enjoyed Obsidian.</a> But Cursed just didn't meet my expectations--and though I usually would have high expectations for such a great author, this time my bars were set to "mediocre" at best, since the premise of Cursed is nothing new and I was worried about clichés. But Jen has this uncanny ability to shift clichés into something actually really, really enjoyable. So why should I be worried?<br /><br />Turns out I was right to worry.<br /><br />Let's take a look at the story: Ember McWilliams, she-who-lost-everything, is suddenly faced with a super hot guy who she just can't seem to resist, despite his father's extreme weirdness.<br /><br />This kind of sounds like Wither, right?<br /><br />Let's look at it again: Ember McWilliams, she-who-suffered-greatly-due-to-a-car-accident, is faced with a dangerous power and a terrifying secret.<br /><br />Hey, why does that remind me of Unraveling?<br /><br />How about one last time: Ember McWilliams's touch is fatal. She then discovers a facility of people like her. And a hot guy. She is now fighting for her life.<br /><br />...Shatter Me and X-Men come to mind...<br /><br />Look. I'm not saying this book isn't original. In fact, though Cursed shares a lot of elements with a lot of amazing books (just like Half-Blood did with Vampire Academy...), it also stands on its own. Ember's situation is much different than Rhine's, her secret has nothing to do with what Janelle discovers, and she's a much more spunky heroine than Juliette. Besides, there are only seven plots under the sky, right?<br /><br />So, no worries. But when your material is not really unique, you have to fall hard on your characters and voice to keep the reader's attention, since now plot twists are extremely easy to guess due to previous interactions with the same situations.<br /><br />Here's usually where Jen shines. Her voice is amazing. Her characters are so true-to-life. It's completely addicting. But... (you were waiting for this "but," weren't you?)<br /><br />I can't really say the same for Cursed.<br /><br />I don't know, maybe writing like five books in one year isn't the best thing to do when faced with detailed narration, or maybe I'm just hallucinating and weird, but the voice in Cursed was not the usual spunk but rather more... dry. The characters are really, really cliché, to be honest. They remind me so much of Twilight and a lot of other books. There were no surprises at all that I got from this book. And with its uncharacteristically mediocre narration and recycled character molds, it's an understatement to say that Cursed didn't meet my expectations.<br /><br />Overall, I do love Jennifer L. Armentrout. I think she's great. Lots of people love Cursed. In fact, I'm one of only three people who rated this book with two stars on Goodreads. So maybe I'm just different. But I think it also needs to be said that I was never an extremely zealous fan, so I approached this book with a here-goes! instead of a more hopeful, optimistic push of an attitude. Maybe this is just me, but alas, I highly recommend going into this book without holding your breath.<br /><br />You never know how you'll feel until you let yourself feel--without being restrained by previous, fangirling infatuations--right?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5986091380670976825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_724756963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724756963" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/724756963?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer724756963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16942710668843123730">I was looking through Jennifer Armentrout's list of books she had written and saw this one. It was published in September, 2012 and I hadn't heard anything about it. I thought it sounded really interesting and boy am I glad I gave it a shot. What a great book! The characters all had so many layers to them. They all had secrets and you just never are sure who to like and who to mistrust. Until the very end. <br/><br/>Ember had a seemingly normal life. She was a normal, angsty teenager, until that fateful n</span>
  <span id="freeText16942710668843123730" style="display:none">I was looking through Jennifer Armentrout's list of books she had written and saw this one. It was published in September, 2012 and I hadn't heard anything about it. I thought it sounded really interesting and boy am I glad I gave it a shot. What a great book! The characters all had so many layers to them. They all had secrets and you just never are sure who to like and who to mistrust. Until the very end. <br /><br />Ember had a seemingly normal life. She was a normal, angsty teenager, until that fateful night. The night when she, her little sister, Olivia, and her parents were in a horrible car accident. Her father died that night and so did she, until her sister Olivia touched her and brought her back to life. That night everything changed.<br /><br />Her Mother physically survives but is never the same. So the responsibility of taking care of her preschool age sister falls on her. But something has changed for Ember as well. Anything she touches dies. Pets, plants, and even people. She will never be able to hold her little sister's hand again. She endures two years like this, trying to go to school, and take care of her sister. But then everything changes, again! And she, her Mom, and Olivia end up at the home of Jonathan Cromwell along with several other teenagers, all with different gifts, that Cromwell has taken in. Mostly, though, there is Hayden, Cromwell's adopted son, that impacts Ember's life. He says he knows her, understands her, and wants to help her to learn to control her gift. And she is drawn to him. She wants to trust him, but can she? Right away things start to happen, bad things. Who is responsible? And, details start to come out about her parents and the accident. Was it really an accident? <br /><br />So many times during this book I thought I knew who was good and who was bad just to have everything change again. It was the perfect balance of suspense and romance between Hayden and Ember. I felt throughout the book that Ember was so strong, to have gone through everything she did and the fact that at her young age she tried so hard to take care of her little sister. I really loved this book and highly recommend it. I knew that I wouldn't be disappointed by anything Jennifer Armentrout writes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16942710668843123730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_227606444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227606444" />
    <a title="Eunice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice"><img alt="Eunice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541224995p2/6078895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227606444?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eunice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eunice" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice">Eunice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=out-2012">out-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=arc-netgalley-edelweiss">arc-netgalley-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227606444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16404881977130187384"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Cursed is a fantastic novel that even though has a pretty common trope - the touch of death - was still able to offer something that is quite different and fresh. And although I did find it not as striking as Armentrout's first two published novels it was still a fairly entertaining read with outstanding characters and fantastic twists. <br/><br/>Embers suffered a lot since the accident that caused his father to die and her to have the ability of touch of death. Her mother had gone into depressio</span>
  <span id="freeText16404881977130187384" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Cursed is a fantastic novel that even though has a pretty common trope - the touch of death - was still able to offer something that is quite different and fresh. And although I did find it not as striking as Armentrout's first two published novels it was still a fairly entertaining read with outstanding characters and fantastic twists. <br /><br />Embers suffered a lot since the accident that caused his father to die and her to have the ability of touch of death. Her mother had gone into depression after that thus leaving her alone to take care of her younger sister, Olivia. Ember is a character that is easy to sympathize with especially with how things turned out for her after the accident - inside and outside of her home. Yet she became a determined and strong-minded character especially when it comes to Olivia. I like how much she cared for her and loved her. But it was also saddening and yes, quite frustrating with how strongly she believed that her ability is a curse - that she is cursed. <br /><br />In all honesty, I was actually really frustrated with her especially with the trust issue she had with Cromwell's group and how <i>long</i> it took her to realized that she'd been wallowing herself for so long and that it was finally time for her to take action and help herself with her ability. Although I think it was already a little late for me to make me like her as much as I did with Katy and Alex, I do still think that she is a person that has a lot of admirable and desirable<br />characteristics. <br /><br />As for the Hayden Cromwell, Ember's love interest and also someone with ability, he is a character that is so easy to like. He is a total sweet heart and although could be described soft if compared to Armentrout's other boys he has this edges in him that makes him definitely crush-able and swoon-worthy. And yes, hot too! His patience and hard work in helping Ember control her gift is admirable and I like how much he loved his adopted family. <br /><br />Overall, this is definitely an entertaining and fantastic read albeit a bit predictable and in my case, quite frustrating. But I can still say that Armentrout's writing is indeed really good because even with those issues I had I can't seem to put this down when I started reading it. This may pale compared to her Obsidian and Half-blood but this book is still a very worthy read. And yes, I guess I treasure this because this is my first ever physical ARC! Haha! I recommend this. <br /><br /><i>Thank you so much Spencer Hill Press for sending me an ARC of this book! You guys rock!</i><br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="http://bookoverdose.blogspot.com/2012/10/title-cursed-author-jennifer-l.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Overdose</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16404881977130187384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_184969682" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184969682" />
    <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books"><img alt="Kayleigh {K-Books}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540157695p2/3996633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184969682?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayleigh {K-Books}" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books">Kayleigh {K-Books}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3996633-kayleigh-k-books?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184969682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10139583394957039558"><a href='http://k-booksxo.blogspot.co.uk/2012/08/review-cursed.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cursed Review on K-Books</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Hayden <u>was</u> kind of drool-worthy. Okay. Not kind of. <u>Definitely</u> drool-worthy."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Wow, I don't even know where to start with this review. Cursed was the first book by Jennifer L Armentrout I ever heard about. It's been added to my must-have list for over a year so you can imagine my excitement when I found out I was getting it for review from the awesome Spencer Hill Press. Since hearing about (and dying to read) Cursed last year I have read all of Jennifer's other books </span>
  <span id="freeText10139583394957039558" style="display:none"><a href="http://k-booksxo.blogspot.co.uk/2012/08/review-cursed.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Cursed Review on K-Books</a><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Hayden <u>was</u> kind of drool-worthy. Okay. Not kind of. <u>Definitely</u> drool-worthy."</i>
</b><br /><br />Wow, I don't even know where to start with this review. Cursed was the first book by Jennifer L Armentrout I ever heard about. It's been added to my must-have list for over a year so you can imagine my excitement when I found out I was getting it for review from the awesome Spencer Hill Press. Since hearing about (and dying to read) Cursed last year I have read all of Jennifer's other books and she is just amazing. I adore both the Lux and Covenant series and have fell in love with her adult book Tempting The Best Man too. I knew Cursed would be incredible. I did not under any circumstances expect it to be this incredible. If I had to describe cursed in one word it would be: Phenomenal!<br /><br />Ember has a gift, well she sees it as more of a Curse. Ever since that fatal accident that left her dead and her gifted sister brought her back she hasn't been able to touch anything living. Her touch is toxic and kills. When Ember meets the mysterious but gorgeous Hayden she thinks he hot (obviously) and crazy but when he suggests there may be a way to control her gift Ember can't help but try. But was the accident that left Ember with this gift really an accident, or is someone still out there after her? <br /><br />I seriously cannot put my thoughts about this book into words. I just want to scream "IT'S AWESOME! READ IT NOW!" When Cursed came through my door this week I started squealing and jumping round like a crazy woman. After reading: I want to squeal and jump round the room like a crazy woman because it is just that phenomenal. Minutes after finishing reading Cursed I wanted to go back to the beginning and read it all again. Jennifer is without a doubt the most amazing author in the world. There is nothing, NOTHING she could ever write that I would absolutely adore and completely obsess over. Cursed is definitely 100% different from all her other books but it is just as addictive and brilliant. I think this really shows her versatility as an author and I am convinced that there is no author in this world that is better than she.<br /><br />Ember is such a fantastic character. I really love her. You really feel for Ember throughout the book. I mean really how could you not. She can't touch anyone. She can't even hold her beloved sister's hand. I think Ember is such a strong character. She breaks down and is very emotional but she is so strong to keep fighting. To keep going and look after her little sister after all the things that has happened to her. If those things had happened to me I'm pretty sure I'd be in a mental institute banging my head of the padded walls.<br /><br />Hayden, oh where do I even start with Hayden. He is just the perfect guy. I definitely have a new book boyfriend. He is so sweet and perfect and he is the character every girl wishes was real and that they'd fall in love with her. He's so adorable. And hot! Very hot! Prepare to drool and swoon and sigh. A LOT! But really what did you expect, all of Jennifer's lead male characters make you drool and swoon and sigh. I have never in my life read such a hot scene where the characters aren't even touching. <br /><br />This book is just phenomenal. It has you guessing what's going to happen and it has so many twists and turns it will leave you dizzy. From the very first page I could not put this book down. It's heart-stopping and exciting and every page leaves you breathless and needing more. I think Cursed is my favourite book of all time, yea not just of Jennifer's but ever. But really no books in the world can top Jennifer's her books are just that good. Cursed is a mind-blowing story that is unputdownable and will stay with you long after you have finished the last page.<br /><br />I cannot praise this book enough. The last thing I will leave you with is this:<br />GO BUY IT NOW! <br />If I could give this book a million stars I would. This book is not to be missed out on. A must-read that I will read over and over again!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"You know my dad has always thought that Olivia was the amazing one, the one who has this remarkable gift. But I've always thought it was you."</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_2118048435" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2118048435" />
    <a title="Maca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52043246-maca"><img alt="Maca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576585322p2/52043246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2118048435?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maca" href="/user/show/52043246-maca">Maca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2118048435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5018785203333565860">I love love love this book ❤️<br/>Okay, not that much but still a lot!<br/>Since I was little I loved movies where were people with superpowers. I think the first movie was X-men and my favorite character was Wolverine (he still is my favorite🥰).<br/>This book has also characters with superpowers and so I had to read it.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564266874ra/27896843.gif' width='350' height='260' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u>Plot</u><br/>The story is mainly about girl Ember who is trying to survive with her 5 years old little sister. They are living with their mum, but she is kind of “crazy”, so Ember has to do almost every</span>
  <span id="freeText5018785203333565860" style="display:none">I love love love this book ❤️<br>Okay, not that much but still a lot!<br>Since I was little I loved movies where were people with superpowers. I think the first movie was X-men and my favorite character was Wolverine (he still is my favorite🥰).<br>This book has also characters with superpowers and so I had to read it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564266874ra/27896843.gif" width="350" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Plot</u><br>The story is mainly about girl Ember who is trying to survive with her 5 years old little sister. They are living with their mum, but she is kind of “crazy”, so Ember has to do almost everything.<br>These sisters have powers. One can kill with touch and the other can raise people from dead.<br>And then one day some shit happens and they are not alone anymore, they are with people who have powers too.<br>But somebody is trying to kill Ember, so who is she going to trust?<br>I suck at explaining story/plot. I swear it’s better than what I just said.<br><br><u>Characters</u><br>I adore these characters 🤩🥰 <br>And especially Hayden. He is such a sweet cinnamon roll. I think he is the only love interest in Armentrout’s books, who is not arrogant jerk.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“You can hate me forever, but it won’t change how I feel.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Ember is awesome person. She is great big sister, she’s brave, smart and I like about her that she is pretty stubborn.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459939270ra/18674844.gif" width="350" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then we have some side characters.<br>Jonathan is a little devil. I think he’s just acting he’s good father but in reality he is not.<br>He is soo shady.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1564266874ra/27896844.gif" width="350" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Phoebe is there to create some drama like she’s the jealous rival. Besides that I understand her other issues and I think she wasn’t bad.<br>Gabe is the “mean” guy who doesn’t like the MC because...who knows? He just doesn’t like her. He is saying he has a reason, but I don’t believe him.<br>Parker - I kinda like him, I guess? I think he could be a very intriguing character if he had more space in the book and if he was more developed.<br><br><u>Writing</u><br>I enjoyed the writing. It was easy, fast-paced and funny read.<br>I know it’s not perfect and maybe not so original but I still like it.<br>I re-read this book a lot. It makes me feel better every time I re-read it when I am in a bad mood 😊😎<br>Damn, why is it not a series? 😭<br>It totally should be, because there are unanswered questions.<br><br>These are my favorite quotes (probably there is more but I can remember only these):<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>”I admitted. If I was going to hallucinate, then at least it was some hot dude instead of something gross.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>”My brain must have felt sorry for me, so it’d created the only type of guy I could touch—a fantasy one.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>„Petersburg was the kind of town people missed if they sneezed.“</i>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>„When you die you feel it empty and leave you.”<br>“Feel what?”(...)<br>“Your soul,” I said quietly. I knew I had told him I didn’t want to talk about it, but here I was with a mad case of verbal diarrhea again. “You feel it burn itself out. Like a candle.“</i>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>„What lies behind you and what lies in front of you, pales in comparison to what lies inside of you.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>”You quoted Oscar Wilde.” I smiled. <br>Hayden laughed. “Yeah, that was, like, the height of geekdom.” <br>“No. It was kind of cool.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>4,25⭐️</span>

<div id="review_1637593133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1637593133" />
    <a title=" Abril Sol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18810241-abril-sol"><img alt=" Abril Sol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592102266p2/18810241.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1637593133?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2016</a>

  <span id="freeText4903339142476060655" style="display:none">Well, this wasn't a literary masterpiece but, as I always say, it's Jennifer L. Armentrout. I can't help but love her books, her stories and romances are always sooooo compelling. I loved the relationship between Ember and Hayden (by the way, I LOVE the name Hayden), he is such a nice guy and eventhough Em was annoying sometimes I could see where all her insecurities came from. <br />This book was very Shatter Me and I was surprised to find out this one was published before Cursed. I'm not saying this is a copy of Shatter Me but I found a lot of remanences to that other book. I loved the fact that this was a stand alone, that's like the best thing about this book, the plot didn't drag so everything flowed just fine. As always, I could not put this book down.<br />Jennifer's book are always a hit for me. I will forever read whatever she publishes. </span>
